JB
Joseph Brown 26.03.2020 00:10:32
What on Earth is Going On?

Abstract:

The talk will briefly cover the way diseases spread in epidemics, what flattening the curve means, and how social distancing helps. ¬†The virus causing COVID-19 is especially deadly because it spreads quickly. ¬†People become infectious before they have symptoms, making social distancing uniquely important for this epidemic. ¬†Its also important that you can behave in a manner that slows the epidemic down even if official orders to behave in the correct fashion have not yet been issued.¬† After a brief talk Dr. Ashlock will take questions.


Biography:

Professor Ashlock is a tenured full professor of mathematics with a Doctorate from CalTech. ¬†He holds the Bioinformatics Chair at the University of Guelph, in Guelph, Ontario, Canada. ¬†He has won multiple awards for research excellence, including the Best Paper award for a paper on modelling epidemics at the 2011 Congress on Evolutionary Computation. ¬†He currently has 302 peer reviewed scientific publications and specializes in designing the presentation of problems to digital systems to make artificial intelligence more effective. ¬†He is a past chair of the IEEE CIS Bioinformatics and Bioengineering Technical Committee and the IEEE CIS Technical Committee on Games. ¬†He is currently an Associate Editor of Biosystems, The IEEE/ACM Transactions on Bioinformatics and Computational Biology, the IEEE Transactions on Evolutionary Computation, and the IEEE Transactions on Games.

This Friday at 4pm - zoom meeting details to follow.

On Covid-19, I strongly recommend this video:
https://youtu.be/gxAaO2rsdIs

One of the takeaways is: in communities with hubs (like Piatchoritka, pharmacay or Magnit), it's a matter of time for the entire population to get infected. My humble suggestion: go as scarcely as possible and buy as much as you can carry when you go supermarket; so you don't need to go again any soon.
